For general graphs, the half-integrality theorem (Nemhauser-Trotter) says optimal LP solution has x_v in {0, 1/2, 1}. Vertices with x_v=1 must be in cover, vertices with x_v=0 cannot, vertices with x_v=1/2 form a subproblem.\n\n### Half-integrality via Crown Reduction:\nTo compute the half-integral LP solution, we can use maximum matching / network flow:\n- Build bipartite graph (left copy L, right copy R of original graph)\n- Find maximum matching\n- Vertices not covered by matching on left side + vertices covered by matching on right side (König\'s theorem in bipartite)\n\nActually for the half-integral LP, we use the Nemhauser-Trotter theorem:\n1. Create bipartite graph B where each vertex v becomes vL and vR\n2. Add edges (uL, vR) and (vL, uR) for each edge (u,v)\n3. Find minimum vertex cover of B (= maximum matching by König)\n4. Vertices in both copies → x=1 (must be in cover)\n5. Vertices in neither copy → x=0 (not in cover)\n6. Vertices in exactly one copy → x=1/2 (undecided)\n\n### Implementation Plan:\n\n1. Read graph\n2. Apply kernelization:\n   a. Remove isolated vertices\n   b. Add degree-1 vertex neighbors to cover, remove them\n   c. Apply NT theorem to get the LP kernel\n3. For the remaining kernel:\n   - If small enough: exact B&B\n   - Otherwise: greedy/local search on the 1/2-vertices\n\n### Branch and Bound:\n- Branch on vertex with maximum degree\n- Upper bound: greedy matching\n- Lower bound: maximum matching size\n- Prune when lower bound >= current best\n\n### For large instances:\nUse greedy matching (take both endpoints) as a 2-approximation, then do local search to improve.\n\nLet me code this up:\n\n```rust\nuse std::io::{self, Read, Write, BufWriter};\nuse std::collections::{VecDeque, HashSet};\n\n// Maximum bipartite matching using Hopcroft-Karp\nstruct HopcroftKarp {\n    n_left: usize,\n    n_right: usize,\n    adj: Vec<Vec<usize>>,\n    match_left: Vec<Option<usize>>,\n    match_right: Vec<Option<usize>>,\n}\n\n// ...\n```\n\nActually, let me think about the large graph case more carefully. right\n    match_left: Vec<usize>, // usize::MAX if unmatched\n    match_right: Vec<usize>,\n    dist: Vec<u32>,\n}\n\nimpl BipartiteGraph {\n    fn new(n_left: usize, n_right: usize) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            n_left,\n            n_right,\n            adj: vec![vec![]; n_left],\n            match_left: vec![usize::MAX; n_left],\n            match_right: vec![usize::MAX; n_right],\n            dist: vec![u32::MAX; n_left + 1],\n        }\n    }\n    \n    fn add_edge(&mut self, u: usize, v: usize) {\n        self.adj[u].push(v);\n    }\n    \n    fn bfs(&mut self) -> bool {\n        let mut queue = VecDeque::new();\n        for u in 0..self.n_left {\n            if self.match_left[u] == usize::MAX {\n                self.dist[u] = 0;\n                queue.push_back(u);\n            } else {\n                self.dist[u] = u32::MAX;\n            }\n        }\n        self.dist[self.n_left] = u32::MAX; // NIL node\n        \n        while let Some(u) = queue.pop_front() {\n            if self.dist[u] < self.dist[self.n_left] {\n                for &v in &self.adj[u].clone() {\n                    let pair_v = self.match_right[v];\n                    let next = if pair_v == usize::MAX { self.n_left } else { pair_v };\n                    if self.dist[next] == u32::MAX {\n                        self.dist[next] = self.dist[u] + 1;\n                        if next != self.n_left {\n                            queue.push_back(next);\n                        }\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n        }\n        self.dist[self.n_left] != u32::MAX\n    }\n    \n    fn dfs(&mut self, u: usize) -> bool {\n        if u == self.n_left { return true; }\n        for i in 0..self.adj[u].len() {\n            let v = self.adj[u][i];\n            let pair_v = self.match_right[v];\n            let next = if pair_v == usize::MAX { self.n_left } else { pair_v };\n            if self.dist[next] == self.dist[u] + 1 && self.dfs(next) {\n                self.match_right[v] = u;\n                self.match_left[u] = v;\n                return true;\n            }\n        }\n        self.dist[u] = u32::MAX;\n        false\n    }\n    \n    fn max_matching(&mut self) -> usize {\n        let mut matching = 0;\n        while self.bfs() {\n            for u in 0..self.n_left {\n                if self.match_left[u] == usize::MAX && self.dfs(u) {\n                    matching += 1;\n                }\n            }\n        }\n        matching\n    }\n    \n    // Find minimum vertex cover using König\'s theorem\n    fn min_vertex_cover(&mut self) -> (Vec<bool>, Vec<bool>) {\n        self.max_matching();\n        \n        // BFS from unmatched left vertices via alternating paths\n        let mut in_z_left = vec![false; self.n_left];\n        let mut in_z_right = vec![false; self.n_right];\n        let mut queue = VecDeque::new();\n        \n        for u in 0..self.n_left {\n            if self.match_left[u] == usize::MAX {\n                in_z_left[u] = true;\n                queue.push_back(u);\n            }\n        }\n        \n        while let Some(u) = queue.pop_front() {\n            for &v in &self.adj[u].clone() {\n                if !in_z_right[v] {\n                    in_z_right[v] = true;\n                    if self.match_right[v] != usize::MAX {\n                        let w = self.match_right[v];\n                        if !in_z_left[w] {\n                            in_z_left[w] = true;\n                            queue.push_back(w);\n                        }\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n        }\n        \n        // Cover = (L \\ Z_L) ∪ (R ∩ Z_R)\n        let cover_left: Vec<bool> = (0..self.n_left).map(|u| !in_z_left[u]).collect();\n        let cover_right: Vec<bool> = (0..self.n_right).map(|v| in_z_right[v]).collect();\n        \n        (cover_left, cover_right)\n    }\n}\n```\n\nNow, for the NT theorem application:\n- We double the graph: for each original The standard FPT algorithm for vertex cover:\n\n```\nvc(G, k):\n  if k < 0: return false\n  if no edges: return true (empty set works)\n  apply reduction rules:\n    - remove isolated vertices\n    - if deg(v) = 1: add neighbor to cover, reduce k by 1, remove both\n    - if deg(v) > k: add v to cover, reduce k by 1, remove v\n    - LP lower bound > k: return false\n  pick edge (u,v) with max degree endpoint u:\n    return vc(G - u, k-1) || vc(G - v, k-1)\n```\n\nThe LP lower bound in each subproblem: compute the LP value for the current subgraph. Since LP is half-integral, LP value = (matching in subgraph) + (number of undecided vertices / 2). The standard LP bound is: sum_{v} x_v >= matching size, so matching_size <= OPT.\n\nFor a simple lower bound: greedy matching size.\n\nFor the B&B in the code, I\'ll:\n1. I\'ll be pragmatic and write working code:\n\n```rust\nuse std::io::{self, Read, Write, BufWriter};\nuse std::collections::VecDeque;\nuse std::time::Instant;\n\nfn main() {\n    let start = Instant::now();\n    \n    // Read input\n    let mut input = String::new();\n    io::stdin().read_to_string(&mut input).unwrap();\n    let mut it = input.split_ascii_whitespace();\n    \n    let n: usize = it.next().unwrap().parse().unwrap();\n    let m: usize = it.next().unwrap().parse().unwrap();\n    \n    let mut edges = Vec::with_capacity(m);\n    for _ in 0..m {\n        let u: usize = it.next().unwrap().parse().unwrap();\n        let v: usize = it.next().unwrap().parse().unwrap();\n        if u != v {\n            edges.push((u, v));\n        }\n    }\n    \n    let mut in_cover = vec![false; n];\n    \n    // Build adjacency lists\n    let mut adj: Vec<Vec<usize>> = vec![vec![]; n];\n    for &(u, v) in &edges {\n        adj[u].push(v);\n        adj[v].push(u);\n    }\n    \n    // Deduplicate adjacency lists\n    for i in 0..n {\n        adj[i].sort_unstable();\n        adj[i].dedup();\n    }\n    \n    let large_n = n > 500_000 || edges.len() > 5_000_000;\n    \n    if large_n {\n        // Greedy + local search\n        greedy_and_local_search(n, &edges, &adj, &mut in_cover, &start);\n    } else {\n        // Full algorithm\n        full_solve(n, &edges, &adj, &mut in_cover, &start);\n    }\n    \n    // Output\n    let stdout = io::stdout();\n    let mut out = BufWriter::new(stdout.lock());\n    let cover: Vec<usize> = (0..n).filter(|&i| in_cover[i]).collect();\n    writeln!(out, "{}", cover.len()).unwrap();\n    let s: Vec<String> = cover.iter().map(|x| x.to_string()).collect();\n    writeln!(out, "{}", s.join(" ")).unwrap();\n}\n```\n\nNow I need to implement `greedy_and_local_search` and `full_solve`.\n\nFor `greedy_and_local_search`:\n1. Greedy matching: iterate edges, if neither endpoint is in cover, add both\n2. Redundancy removal: repeatedly remove vertices from cover where all their edges are doubly covered\n\nActually, step 2 is: if v is in cover and removing v still keeps all edges covered (i.e., for every edge (v,u), u is also in cover), then remove v.\n\n```rust\nfn greedy_and_local_search(\n    n: usize,\n    edges: &[(usize, usize)],\n    adj: &[Vec<usize>],\n    in_cover: &mut Vec<bool>,\n    start: &Instant,\n) {\n    // Greedy matching\n    for &(u, v) in edges {\n        if !in_cover[u] && !in_cover[v] {\n            in_cover[u] = true;\n            in_cover[v] = true;\n        }\n    }\n    \n    // Redundancy removal\n    let mut changed = true;\n    while changed && start.elapsed().as_millis() < 8000 {\n        changed = false;\n        for v in 0..n {\n            if in_cover[v] {\n                let redundant = adj[v].iter().all(|&u| in_cover[u]);\n                if redundant {\n                    in_cover[v] = false;\n                    changed = true;\n                }\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\nFor `full_solve`:\n1. I\'ll use an explicit representation with:\n- `active: Vec<bool>` for vertices\n- `deg: Vec<usize>` for degrees (of active edges to active vertices)\n- `in_cover: Vec<bool>` for current cover assignment\n\nWhen adding vertex v to cover:\n- Mark v as in_cover\n- For each active neighbor u of v, decrease deg[u]\n- Remove all edges incident to v\n\nWhen removing vertex v from cover (backtrack):\n- Restore v\'s active status\n- Restore all edges incident to v\n- Increase degrees of neighbors\n\nThis requires careful tracking of what changed.\n\nAlternatively, for simplicity, I can just work with adjacency lists and copy the active set when branching. Better: use explicit undo operations.\n\nLet me use the "remove/add vertex" operations with undo stacks:\n\n```rust\nstruct BnBState {\n    n: usize,\n    adj: Vec<Vec<usize>>,\n    active: Vec<bool>,\n    in_cover: Vec<bool>,\n    deg: Vec<usize>, // degree counting only active neighbors\n}\n\nimpl BnBState {\n    fn remove_vertex(&mut self, v: usize, was_active: &mut Vec<usize>) {\n        was_active.push(v);\n        self.active[v] = false;\n        for &u in &self.adj[v] {\n            if self.active[u] {\n                self.deg[u] -= 1;\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    \n    fn restore_vertex(&mut self, v: usize) {\n        self.active[v] = true;\n        for &u in &self.adj[v] {\n            if self.active[u] {\n                self.deg[u] += 1;\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    \n    fn branch(&mut self, k: usize, current_size: usize, best: &mut usize, best_cover: &mut Vec<bool>) {\n        // Apply reductions\n        let mut undo_stack: Vec<(usize, bool)> = vec![]; // (vertex, was_added_to_cover)\n        \n        loop {\n            // Remove isolated vertices\n            let mut found = false;\n            for v in 0..self.n {\n                if self.active[v] && self.deg[v] == 0 {\n                    self.remove_vertex(v, &mut vec![]);\n                    undo_stack.push((v, false));\n                    found = true;\n                }\n            }\n            // Handle degree-1 vertices\n            let mut deg1 = None;\n            for v in 0..self.n {\n                if self.active[v] && self.deg[v] == 1 {\n                    deg1 = Some(v);\n                    break;\n                }\n            }\n            if let Some(v) = deg1 {\n                // Find neighbor\n                let u = self.adj[v].iter().find(|&&u| self.active[u]).copied().unwrap();\n                // Add u to cover\n                self.in_cover[u] = true;\n                undo_stack.push((u, true));\n                // Remove u and v\n                self.remove_vertex(u, &mut vec![]);\n                self.remove_vertex(v, &mut vec![]);\n                undo_stack.push((v, false));\n                // Also remove all of u\'s neighbors edges (they\'re covered)\n                // ...\n                found = true;\n            }\n            if !found { break; }\n        }\n        \n        // ...\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis is getting complex. Let me simplify by using a clean recursive B&B:\n\n```rust\n// Returns the minimum number of vertices needed to cover the graph\n// represented by active vertices and their adjacency\n// Adds chosen vertices to in_cover\nfn bb(\n    adj: &Vec<Vec<usize>>,\n    active: &mut Vec<bool>,\n    deg: &mut Vec<usize>,\n    in_cover: &mut Vec<bool>,\n    k: usize, // remaining budget\n    best: &mut usize,\n    best_cover: &mut Vec<bool>,\n    start: &Instant,\n) {\n    if start.elapsed().as_millis() > TIME_LIMIT_MS {\n        return;\n    }\n    \n    // Apply reduction rules\n    let mut added = vec![];\n    let mut removed = vec![];\n    \n    // Rule 1: remove isolated vertices\n    // Rule 2: degree-1 vertices - add neighbor\n    // Rule 3: if deg(v) > k, add v\n    \n    // ...\n    \n    // Find uncovered edge\n    let max_deg_vertex = (0..n).filter(|&v| active[v]).max_by_key(|&v| deg[v]);\n    \n    if let Some(v) = max_deg_vertex {\n        if deg[v] == 0 {\n            // All edges covered\n            let size = in_cover.iter().filter(|&&b| b).count();\n            if size < *best {\n                *best = size;\n                *best_cover = in_cover.clone();\n            }\n        } else {\n            // Branch on v\n            // Option 1: include v\n            // Option 2: include all neighbors of v\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\nOK, this is getting quite involved. Actually, the standard Hopcroft-Karp implementation uses a work array to avoid re-traversing edges.\n\nLet me use the standard Hopcroft-Karp with work array:\n\n```rust\nfn hopcroft_karp(adj: &[Vec<usize>], n_left: usize, n_right: usize) -> (Vec<usize>, Vec<usize>) {\n    let mut match_l = vec![usize::MAX; n_left];\n    let mut match_r = vec![usize::MAX; n_right];\n    let inf = u32::MAX;\n    let nil = n_left; // sentinel\n    let mut dist = vec![inf; n_left + 1];\n    \n    loop {\n        // BFS\n        let mut queue = VecDeque::new();\n        for u in 0..n_left {\n            if match_l[u] == usize::MAX {\n                dist[u] = 0;\n                queue.push_back(u);\n            } else {\n                dist[u] = inf;\n            }\n        }\n        dist[nil] = inf;\n        while let Some(u) = queue.pop_front() {\n            if dist[u] < dist[nil] {\n                for &v in &adj[u] {\n                    let w = if match_r[v] == usize::MAX { nil } else { match_r[v] };\n                    if dist[w] == inf {\n                        dist[w] = dist[u] + 1;\n                        if w != nil {\n                            queue.push_back(w);\n                        }\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n        }\n        if dist[nil] == inf { break; }\n        \n        // DFS for each unmatched left vertex\n        let mut work = (0..n_left).map(|u| adj[u].len()).collect::<Vec<_>>();\n        // Actually need index into adj, not length\n        // Use a work pointer\n        let mut work_ptr = vec![0usize; n_left];\n        \n        for u in 0..n_left {\n            if match_l[u] == usize::MAX {\n                dfs_hk(u, &adj, &mut match_l, &mut match_r, &mut dist, &mut work_ptr, nil);\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    \n    (match_l, match_r)\n}\n```\n\nHmm, the DFS also needs to be careful. Let me use the iterative version or just the standard recursive one.\n\nFor the final solution, let me just write clean recursive Hopcroft-Karp with work pointers to avoid re-traversing edges:\n\n```rust\nfn dfs_hk(\n    u: usize,\n    adj: &[Vec<usize>],\n    match_l: &mut Vec<usize>,\n    match_r: &mut Vec<usize>,\n    dist: &mut Vec<u32>,\n    work: &mut Vec<usize>,\n    nil: usize,\n) -> bool {\n    if u == nil { return true; }\n    while work[u] < adj[u].len() {\n        let v = adj[u][work[u]];\n        let w = if match_r[v] == usize::MAX { nil } else { match_r[v] };\n        if dist[w] == dist[u] + 1 && dfs_hk(w, adj, match_l, match_r, dist, work, nil) {\n            match_r[v] = u;\n            match_l[u] = v;\n            return true;\n        }\n        work[u] += 1;\n    }\n    dist[u] = u32::MAX;\n    false\n}\n```\n\nBut this has unbounded recursion depth (up to n). I\'ll keep it pragmatic.\n\nHere\'s my implementation:\n\n```rust\nuse std::collections::VecDeque;\nuse std::io::{self, Read, Write, BufWriter};\nuse std::time::Instant;\n\nfn main() {\n    let builder = std::thread::Builder::new().stack_size(64 * 1024 * 1024);\n    let handler = builder.spawn(actual_main).unwrap();\n    handler.join().unwrap();\n}\n\nfn actual_main() {\n    let start = Instant::now();\n    let stdout = io::stdout();\n    let mut out = BufWriter::new(stdout.lock());\n    \n    let mut input = String::new();\n    io::stdin().read_to_string(&mut input).unwrap();\n    let mut it = input.split_ascii_whitespace();\n    \n    let n: usize = it.next().unwrap().parse().unwrap();\n    let m: usize = it.next().unwrap().parse().unwrap();\n    \n    let mut raw_edges = Vec::with_capacity(m);\n    for _ in 0..m {\n        let u: usize = it.next().unwrap().parse().unwrap();\n        let v: usize = it.next().unwrap().parse().unwrap();\n        if u != v {\n            raw_edges.push((u.min(v), u.max(v)));\n        }\n    }\n    // Remove duplicate edges\n    raw_edges.sort_unstable();\n    raw_edges.dedup();\n    \n    let mut adj: Vec<Vec<usize>> = vec![vec![]; Let me now think about the NT theorem.\n\n**NT theorem implementation:**\n- Create bipartite graph with n_left = n_right = n (original vertices)\n- For each original edge (u, v), add bipartite edges:\n  - (u, v+n) [u in left connects to v in right]\n  - (v, u+n) [v in left connects to u in right]\n  Wait, I\'m using L copies as 0..n and R copies as 0..n in separate spaces\n- Run Hopcroft-Karp\n- Find min vertex cover of bipartite graph (König\'s theorem)\n- Map back to original vertices\n\nFor mapping: vertex v in original graph:\n- left vertex = v (index in left side)\n- right vertex = v (index in right side)\n- cover_left[v] = left v is in bipartite cover\n- cover_right[v] = right v is in bipartite cover\n\nClassification:\n- cover_left[v] AND cover_right[v]: x=1 (must include)\n- !cover_left[v] AND !cover_right[v]: x=0 (must exclude)\n- Otherwise: x=1/2 (undecided)\n\nBut we need to verify this is correct. The NT theorem states that there exists an optimal VC containing all x=1 vertices and no x=0 vertices. The x=1/2 vertices form a subgraph where we need to find the VC.\n\nNow, for the undecided subgraph: we only consider edges where both endpoints are undecided. We also add edges where one endpoint is x=0 and the other is x=1/2... wait, actually for edges (u,v):\n- If u has x=0 and v has x=1: covered by v (v is in cover)\n- If u has x=0 and v has x=1/2: v must be in cover (since u isn\'t). But this would mean v should be x=1, not x=1/2.\n\nHmm, let me think again. The NT classification guarantees that:\n- All edges with at least one endpoint with x=1 are covered\n- For edges with both endpoints x=1/2, we need to solve the subproblem\n- There should be no edge with x=0 endpoint unless the other endpoint has x >= 1/2... \n\nActually, the LP constraint says x_u + x_v >= 1. With the half-integral solution:\n- If x_u = 0 and x_v = 0: not possible (violates constraint)\n- If x_u = 0 and x_v = 1/2: 0 + 1/2 = 1/2 < 1, violates constraint!\n\nWait, that\'s not right either. Let me re-read the NT theorem.\n\nThe Nemhauser-Trotter theorem (1975):\nFor the LP relaxation of vertex cover (minimize sum x_v, subject to x_u + x_v >= 1 for all edges, 0 <= x_v <= 1), there is always an optimal half-integral solution (all x_v in {0, 1/2, 1}).\n\nFurthermore, we can find an optimal integral solution by:\n1. Taking all vertices with x_v = 1\n2. Solving the subproblem on vertices with x_v = 1/2 (both endpoints must be 1/2 for an edge to be in the subproblem)\n\nFor edges with x_u = 0 and x_v = ?: In a valid LP solution, x_u + x_v >= 1, so if x_u = 0, then x_v >= 1, meaning x_v = 1. So there are no edges between x=0 and x=1/2 vertices! This confirms that the subgraph on x=1/2 vertices is well-defined.\n\nSo the classification from the doubled bipartite graph should correctly classify all edges as either:\n- Both endpoints x=1 (covered by both in cover - fine, we take both)\n- One endpoint x=1, one x=1/2 or x=0 (covered by the x=1 endpoint)\n- Both endpoints x=1/2 (must solve subproblem)\n- Both endpoints x=0: impossible!\n\nWait, but there CAN be edges between x=0 and x=1/2 if the LP solution is not optimal... Actually no, the LP constraint must be satisfied. Let me think: if x_u = 0 and x_v = 1/2, then x_u + x_v = 1/2 < 1, which violates the LP constraint. So in a valid LP solution, this cannot happen.\n\nSo the NT theorem guarantees:\n1. No edge has both endpoints x=0\n2. No edge has one endpoint x=0 and the other x=1/2\n3. All edges between x=1/2 vertices form the subproblem\n4. Adding all x=1 vertices to the cover and optimally solving the subproblem gives an optimal solution\n\nNow, to find the half-integral LP solution using the doubled bipartite graph:\n- Build bipartite graph with left copies L and right copies R of original vertices\n- For each original edge (u,v), add bipartite edges (u_L, v_R) and (v_L, u_R)\n- Find minimum vertex cover of bipartite graph (König\'s = max matching)\n- Map: v has x=1 if v_L in cover AND v_R in cover\n       v has x=0 if v_L not in cover AND v_R not in cover\n       v has x=1/2 otherwise\n\nThis is the standard approach. Let me verify with a simple example:\n- Triangle (0,1,2): optimal VC = {0,1} or any 2 vertices (OPT=2), LP value = 3/2\n- Doubled bipartite graph: L={0_L, 1_L, 2_L}, R={0_R, 1_R, 2_R}\n  Edges: (0_L,1_R), (1_L,0_R), (1_L,2_R), (2_L,1_R), (0_L,2_R), (2_L,0_R)\n- This is a complete bipartite graph K_{3,3}! NT should give x=1/2 for all vertices in a triangle\n\nHmm, something is off. One such cover is all left vertices (cover = {0_L, 1_L, 2_L}) or all right vertices.\n\nIf cover = all left = {0_L, 1_L, 2_L} and no right vertices:\n- v_L in cover, v_R not in cover for all v\n- So all v have x = 1/2\n\nThat makes sense for a triangle! The LP value would be 3 * 1/2 = 3/2, and the minimum VC of the triangle is 2.\n\nSo the König\'s algorithm needs to find the RIGHT minimum vertex cover of the bipartite graph that corresponds to the half-integral LP solution.\n\nThe König\'s theorem algorithm finds a specific minimum VC based on BFS from unmatched left vertices. The specific VC found may or may not correspond to the half-integral LP solution in the "correct" way.\n\nLet me re-examine. For K_{3,3} with a perfect matching M = {(0_L,0_R), (1_L,1_R), (2_L,2_R)}:\n- All left vertices are matched\n- BFS from unmatched left vertices: empty set\n- Z_L = ∅, Z_R = ∅\n- Cover = (L \\ Z_L) ∪ (R ∩ Z_R) = L ∪ ∅ = {0_L, 1_L, 2_L}\n\nSo cover_left = [true, true, true], cover_right = [false, false, false].\n- For original vertex v: cover_left[v]=true, cover_right[v]=false → x=1/2 ✓\n\nBut what if matching is M = {(0_L,1_R), (1_L,2_R), (2_L,0_R)}?\n- BFS from unmatched left: none\n- Z_L = ∅, Z_R = ∅\n- Cover = L = {0_L, 1_L, 2_L}\n- Same result: all x=1/2 ✓\n\nOK so the algorithm works. My earlier confusion was wrong. For the triangle, all vertices get x=1/2, and the minimum VC has size 2 vs. LP lower bound of 3/2. The B&B on the undecided subgraph will find the optimal.\n\nLet me also verify for a graph with a clear x=1 vertex:\n- Star K_{1,3}: center vertex 0, leaves 1,2,3\n- Optimal VC = {0} (size 1), LP value = 1\n- Doubled bipartite graph:\n  Edges: (0_L,1_R),(1_L,0_R), (0_L,2_R),(2_L,0_R), (0_L,3_R),(3_L,0_R)\n  So left vertex 0 connects to {1_R,2_R,3_R}, left vertices 1,2,3 each connect to {0_R}\n- Max matching: match (0_L,1_R), (1_L,0_R) → wait, that\'s only 2 matches. Now let me code this up properly.\n\nFor the overall algorithm:\n\n1. Kernelize: remove degree-0 vertices, add neighbors of degree-1 vertices to cover\n2. On remaining kernel: apply NT (Hopcroft-Karp + König\'s)\n3. Let me write it now:\n\nI\'ll structure the code as follows:\n- `main()`: spawn thread with large stack\n- `run()`: read input, decide algorithm, output\n- `kernelize()`: degree-0 and degree-1 reduction\n- `nt_theorem()`: apply NT theorem using Hopcroft-Karp\n- `hopcroft_karp()`: find max bipartite matching\n- `konig_cover()`: find min vertex cover from matching\n- `branch_and_bound()`: exact B&B for small graphs\n- `greedy_vc()`: greedy matching approximation\n- `remove_redundant()`: remove redundant vertices from cover\n\nLet me now write the final code. I\'ll be very careful about:\n1. Off-by-one errors\n2. Borrow checker issues (avoid re-borrowing)\n3. Stack overflow (use thread with large stack)\n4. Compilation warnings (no unused variables)\n\nHere\'s the code:\n\n```rust\nuse std::collections::VecDeque;\nuse std::io::{self, Read, Write, BufWriter};\nuse std::time::Instant;\n\nfn main() {\n    let builder = std::thread::Builder::new().stack_size(256 * 1024 * 1024);\n    let handler = builder.spawn(run).unwrap();\n    handler.join().unwrap();\n}\n\nfn run() {\n    let start = Instant::now();\n    let mut input = String::new();\n    io::stdin().read_to_string(&mut input).unwrap();\n    let mut it = input.split_ascii_whitespace();\n    \n    macro_rules! next {\n        ($t:ty) => { it.next().unwrap().parse::<$t>().unwrap() }\n    }\n    \n    let n = next!(usize);\n    let m = next!(usize);\n    \n    let mut raw_edges: Vec<(usize, usize)> = Vec::with_capacity(m);\n    for _ in 0..m {\n        let u = next!(usize);\n        let v = next!(usize);\n        if u != v {\n            raw_edges.push((u.min(v), u.max(v)));\n        }\n    }\n    raw_edges.sort_unstable();\n    raw_edges.dedup();\n    let m_actual = raw_edges.len();\n    \n    let mut adj: Vec<Vec<usize>> = vec![vec![]; n];\n    for &(u, v) in &raw_edges {\n        adj[u].push(v);\n        adj[v].push(u);\n    }\n    \n    let mut active = vec![true; n];\n    let mut deg: Vec<usize> = (0..n).map(|v| adj[v].len()).collect();\n    let mut in_cover = vec![false; n];\n    \n    // Phase 1: Kernelization\n    kernelize(n, &adj, &mut active, &mut deg, &mut in_cover);\n    \n    // Count remaining active vertices and edges\n    let active_n: usize = active.iter().filter(|&&a| a).count();\n    // active_m: edges between active vertices (each edge counted once)\n    let active_m: usize = (0..n)\n        .filter(|&v| active[v])\n        .map(|v| adj[v].iter().filter(|&&u| active[u]).count())\n        .sum::<usize>() / 2;\n    \n    // Decide algorithm\n    let use_nt = active_n <= 200_000 && active_m <= 3_000_000;\n    let use_exact_bb = !use_nt || active_n > 500; // fallback\n    \n    if active_n == 0 {\n        // All done by kernelization\n    } else if use_nt && active_n <= 200_000 {\n        // Apply NT theorem\n        let (x1_vertices, x_half_vertices, sub_adj) = nt_theorem(\n            n, &adj, &active, &deg\n        );\n        \n        // Add x=1 vertices to cover\n        for &v in &x1_vertices {\n            in_cover[v] = true;\n        }\n        \n        // Now solve the subproblem on x=1/2 vertices\n        if !x_half_vertices.is_empty() {\n            let sub_n = x_half_vertices.len();\n            // Map original vertices to subgraph indices\n            let mut to_sub = vec![usize::MAX; n];\n            for (i, &v) in x_half_vertices.iter().enumerate() {\n                to_sub[v] = i;\n            }\n            \n            if sub_n <= 300 || start.elapsed().as_millis() < 3000 {\n                // Use B&B\n                let sub_cover = bb_solve(sub_n, &sub_adj, &start);\n                for (i, &in_c) in sub_cover.iter().enumerate() {\n                    if in_c {\n                        in_cover[x_half_vertices[i]] = true;\n                    }\n                }\n            } else {\n                // Greedy on subgraph\n                let mut sub_in_cover = vec![false; sub_n];\n                greedy_vc(sub_n, &sub_adj, &mut sub_in_cover);\n                remove_redundant(sub_n, &sub_adj, &mut sub_in_cover);\n                for (i, &in_c) in sub_in_cover.iter().enumerate() {\n                    if in_c {\n                        in_cover[x_half_vertices[i]] = true;\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n        }\n    } else {\n        // Large graph or NT skipped: greedy + local search\n        let mut sub_active = active.clone();\n        let mut sub_deg = deg.clone();\n        // Another round of kernelization (already done)\n        greedy_vc_active(n, &adj, &sub_active, &sub_deg, &mut in_cover);\n        remove_redundant_active(n, &adj, &active, &mut in_cover);\n    }\n    \n    // Verify (debug)\n    #[cfg(debug_assertions)]\n    {\n        for &(u, v) in &raw_edges {\n            assert!(in_cover[u] || in_cover[v], "Edge ({},{}) not covered!", u, v);\n        }\n    }\n    \n    // Output\n    let stdout = io::stdout();\n    let mut out = BufWriter::new(stdout.lock());\n    let cover: Vec<usize> = (0..n).filter(|&i| in_cover[i]).collect();\n    writeln!(out, "{}", cover.len()).unwrap();\n    if cover.is_empty() {\n        writeln!(out, "").unwrap();\n    } else {\n        let s: Vec<String> = cover.iter().map(|x| x.to_string()).collect();\n        writeln!(out, "{}", s.join(" ")).unwrap();\n    }\n}\n```\n\nNow I need to implement:\n1. `kernelize()`\n2. `nt_theorem()`  \n3. `hopcroft_karp()`\n4. `bb_solve()`\n5. `greedy_vc()`\n6. `remove_redundant()`\n\nLet me write each one:\n\n### `kernelize()`\n```rust\nfn kernelize(\n    n: usize,\n    adj: &[Vec<usize>],\n    active: &mut Vec<bool>,\n    deg: &mut Vec<usize>,\n    in_cover: &mut Vec<bool>,\n) {\n    let mut queue = VecDeque::new();\n    for v in 0..n {\n        if active[v] && deg[v] <= 1 {\n            queue.push_back(v);\n        }\n    }\n    \n    while let Some(v) = queue.pop_front() {\n        if !active[v] { continue; }\n        \n        if deg[v] == 0 {\n            active[v] = false;\n        } else if deg[v] == 1 {\n            // Find active neighbor\n            let u = adj[v].iter().find(|&&u| active[u]).copied();\n            if let Some(u) = u {\n                // Add u to cover, remove both u and v\n                in_cover[u] = true;\n                active[u] = false;\n                active[v] = false;\n                \n                // Update u\'s active neighbors\' degrees\n                for &w in &adj[u] {\n                    if active[w] {\n                        deg[w] -= 1;\n                        if deg[w] <= 1 {\n                            queue.push_back(w);\n                        }\n                    }\n                }\n                // Note: v\'s degree doesn\'t matter since v is deactivated\n                // But we don\'t need to update v\'s neighbors since only u was v\'s active neighbor\n                // Actually, we should decrease deg of v\'s other active neighbors if any\n                // Since deg[v] == 1, v only has one active neighbor (u), and u is now deactivated\n                // So no other neighbors to update for v\n            } else {\n                active[v] = false; // isolated\n            }\n        }\n        // else deg[v] > 1: leave in kernel\n    }\n}\n```\n\nWait, there\'s a subtle issue. When we deactivate u, we didn\'t decrease deg for v (since v is also being deactivated). But deg[v] = 1, so u was v\'s only active neighbor. After removing u, deg[v] would become 0, and v would become isolated. But we\'re already removing v too, so that\'s fine.\n\nHowever, when we remove u, we should also update deg for v (it becomes 0). But since we\'re also removing v in the same step, this is OK.\n\nThe issue is: when we process u\'s neighbors (excluding v which is already deactivated), we update their degrees. But wait, we check `if active[w]` in the loop `for &w in &adj[u]`. Since v is already deactivated (`active[v] = false`), it won\'t be processed. ✓\n\nBut there\'s another issue: when we process the degree-1 vertex v and add u (its neighbor) to the cover, we need to remove u from the graph. This means removing all edges incident to u. In the degree array, this means decreasing the degree of all active neighbors of u. We do this in the loop. ✓\n\nBut we also need to handle the case where v has degree > 1 but is in the queue (because we added it when its degree was 1). The `if !active[v]` check handles already-removed vertices. ✓\n\nHmm, but what if v\'s degree dropped to 1, we queued it, then later it dropped to 0? If deg has decreased further to 0 by the time we dequeue, we handle deg[v]==0 separately. ✓\n\nOne more issue: when we dequeue v and deg[v] == 2 or more (because something we thought would reduce it didn\'t), we skip it (since none of the conditions match). But we won\'t add it back to the queue, so it stays in the kernel. ✓\n\nI think the logic is correct. Let me move on.\n\n### `nt_theorem()`\n\nThis applies the NT theorem:\n\n```rust\nfn nt_theorem(\n    n: usize,\n    adj: &[Vec<usize>],\n    active: &[bool],\n    _deg: &[usize],\n) -> (Vec<usize>, Vec<usize>, Vec<Vec<usize>>) {\n    // Build bipartite graph\n    // Left: 0..n (representing original vertices in left copy)\n    // Right: 0..n (representing original vertices in right copy)\n    // Only active vertices\n    \n    // Collect active vertices and map them\n    let active_verts: Vec<usize> = (0..n).filter(|&v| active[v]).collect();\n    let n_active = active_verts.len();\n    let mut to_idx = vec![usize::MAX; n];\n    for (i, &v) in active_verts.iter().enumerate() {\n        to_idx[v] = i;\n    }\n    \n    // Build bipartite adjacency (left index -> list of right indices)\n    let mut bi_adj: Vec<Vec<usize>> = vec![vec![]; n_active];\n    for &v in &active_verts {\n        let vi = to_idx[v];\n        for &u in &adj[v] {\n            if active[u] {\n                let ui = to_idx[u];\n                // Edge (v, u) → bipartite edges (vi_L, ui_R) and (ui_L, vi_R)\n                bi_adj[vi].push(ui); // vi in left connects to ui in right\n                // We\'ll add the reverse when processing ui\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    // Wait, we need to add BOTH (vi, ui_R) and (ui, vi_R) for each original edge (v,u)\n    // Since adj[v] contains u and adj[u] contains v, when we process v we add vi->ui,\n    // and when we process u we add ui->vi. So bi_adj[vi] will contain ui AND bi_adj[ui] will contain vi.\n    // This means vi_L connects to ui_R AND ui_L connects to vi_R. ✓\n    \n    // Find max matching using Hopcroft-Karp\n    let (match_l, match_r) = hopcroft_karp(&bi_adj, n_active, n_active);\n    \n    // Find min vertex cover using König\'s theorem\n    let (cover_l, cover_r) = konig_cover(&bi_adj, n_active, n_active, &match_l, &match_r);\n    \n    // Classify active vertices\n    let mut x1_verts = vec![];\n    let mut x_half_verts = vec![];\n    \n    for &v in &active_verts {\n        let vi = to_idx[v];\n        match (cover_l[vi], cover_r[vi]) {\n            (true, true) => x1_verts.push(v),\n            (false, false) => (), // x=0, not in cover\n            _ => x_half_verts.push(v), // x=1/2, undecided\n        }\n    }\n    \n    // Build subgraph for x=1/2 vertices\n    let sub_n = x_half_verts.len();\n    let mut sub_to_idx = vec![usize::MAX; n];\n    for (i, &v) in x_half_verts.iter().enumerate() {\n        sub_to_idx[v] = i;\n    }\n    \n    let mut sub_adj = vec![vec![]; sub_n];\n    for &v in &x_half_verts {\n        let vi = sub_to_idx[v];\n        for &u in &adj[v] {\n            if active[u] && sub_to_idx[u] != usize::MAX {\n                let ui = sub_to_idx[u];\n                if vi < ui { // add each edge once\n                    sub_adj[vi].push(ui);\n                    sub_adj[ui].push(vi);\n                }\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    \n    (x1_verts, x_half_verts, sub_adj)\n}\n```\n\nHm wait, I have a bug in the bipartite adj construction. When I do:\n```\nfor &v in &active_verts {\n    let vi = to_idx[v];\n    for &u in &adj[v] {\n        if active[u] {\n            let ui = to_idx[u];\n            bi_adj[vi].push(ui);\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\nSince adj[v] contains u and adj[u] contains v:\n- When processing v: bi_adj[vi].push(ui) → vi_L connects to ui_R\n- When processing u: bi_adj[ui].push(vi) → ui_L connects to vi_R\n\nFor each original edge (v,u), we need:\n- bi_adj[vi].push(ui): vi in left connects to ui in right\n- bi_adj[ui].push(vi): ui in left connects to vi in right\n\nSince adj[v] has u and adj[u] has v (it\'s undirected), both are added automatically. ✓\n\nBut I need to check: are there duplicate edges? If original adj has duplicates (we deduped earlier), then no. ✓\n\nActually wait, I\'m adding edges from v_L to u_R, and the bi_adj[v] represents the left vertex v_L\'s neighbors in the right side. So bi_adj[v][i] = u means there\'s an edge from v_L to u_R. When processing original edge (v,u):\n- Process v: bi_adj[vi].push(ui) → v_L → u_R ✓\n- Process u: bi_adj[ui].push(vi) → u_L → v_R ✓\n\nThis correctly creates both bipartite edges for each original edge. ✓\n\n### `hopcroft_karp()`\n\n```rust\nfn hopcroft_karp(adj: &[Vec<usize>], n_left: usize, n_right: usize) -> (Vec<usize>, Vec<usize>) {\n    let nil = n_left;\n    let mut match_l = vec![usize::MAX; n_left];\n    let mut match_r = vec![usize::MAX; n_right];\n    let mut dist = vec![u32::MAX; n_left + 1];\n    \n    loop {\n        // BFS phase\n        let mut queue = VecDeque::new();\n        for u in 0..n_left {\n            if match_l[u] == usize::MAX {\n                dist[u] = 0;\n                queue.push_back(u);\n            } else {\n                dist[u] = u32::MAX;\n            }\n        }\n        dist[nil] = u32::MAX;\n        \n        while let Some(u) = queue.pop_front() {\n            if dist[u] < dist[nil] {\n                for &v in &adj[u] {\n                    let next = if match_r[v] == usize::MAX { nil } else { match_r[v] };\n                    if dist[next] == u32::MAX {\n                        dist[next] = dist[u] + 1;\n                        if next != nil {\n                            queue.push_back(next);\n                        }\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n        }\n        \n        if dist[nil] == u32::MAX { break; }\n        \n        // DFS phase\n        let mut work = vec![0usize; n_left];\n        for u in 0..n_left {\n            if match_l[u] == usize::MAX {\n                dfs_hk(u, adj, &mut match_l, &mut match_r, &mut dist, &mut work, nil);\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    \n    (match_l, match_r)\n}\n\nfn dfs_hk(\n    u: usize,\n    adj: &[Vec<usize>],\n    match_l: &mut Vec<usize>,\n    match_r: &mut Vec<usize>,\n    dist: &mut Vec<u32>,\n    work: &mut Vec<usize>,\n    nil: usize,\n) -> bool {\n    if u == nil { return true; }\n    while work[u] < adj[u].len() {\n        let v = adj[u][work[u]];\n        let next = if match_r[v] == usize::MAX { nil } else { match_r[v] };\n        if dist[next] == dist[u] + 1 && dfs_hk(next, adj, match_l, match_r, dist, work, nil) {\n            match_r[v] = u;\n            match_l[u] = v;\n            return true;\n        }\n        work[u] += 1;\n    }\n    dist[u] = u32::MAX;\n    false\n}\n```\n\n### `konig_cover()`\n\n```rust\nfn konig_cover(\n    adj: &[Vec<usize>],\n    n_left: usize,\n    n_right: usize,\n    match_l: &[usize],\n    match_r: &[usize],\n) -> (Vec<bool>, Vec<bool>) {\n    let mut in_z_left = vec![false; n_left];\n    let mut in_z_right = vec![false; n_right];\n    let mut queue = VecDeque::new();\n    \n    // Start from unmatched left vertices\n    for u in 0..n_left {\n        if match_l[u] == usize::MAX {\n            in_z_left[u] = true;\n            queue.push_back(u);\n        }\n    }\n    \n    while let Some(u) = queue.pop_front() {\n        for &v in &adj[u] {\n            if !in_z_right[v] {\n                in_z_right[v] = true;\n                // Follow matching edge from v to left\n                if match_r[v] != usize::MAX {\n                    let w = match_r[v];\n                    if !in_z_left[w] {\n                        in_z_left[w] = true;\n                        queue.push_back(w);\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    \n    // Cover = (L \\ Z_L) ∪ (R ∩ Z_R)\n    let cover_l: Vec<bool> = (0..n_left).map(|u| !in_z_left[u]).collect();\n    let cover_r: Vec<bool> = (0..n_right).map(|v| in_z_right[v]).collect();\n    \n    (cover_l, cover_r)\n}\n```\n\n### `bb_solve()` - Branch and Bound\n\nFor the B&B, I\'ll use the following approach:\n- Maintain active vertices and their degrees\n- Apply reduction rules (degree-0, degree-1, degree > k)\n- Branch on the vertex with maximum degree\n- Use a greedy matching as lower bound\n\n```rust\nstruct BBState {\n    n: usize,\n    adj: Vec<Vec<usize>>,\n    active: Vec<bool>,\n    deg: Vec<usize>,\n    in_cover: Vec<bool>,\n    current_cover_size: usize,\n    best_cover_size: usize,\n    best_cover: Vec<bool>,\n}\n\nimpl BBState {\n    fn new(n: usize, adj: Vec<Vec<usize>>) -> Self {\n        let deg: Vec<usize> = (0..n).map(|v| adj[v].len()).collect();\n        let best_cover_size = n; // worst case\n        let best_cover = vec![true; n]; // everyone in cover\n        // Actually compute a greedy upper bound\n        BBState {\n            n,\n            adj,\n            active: vec![true; n],\n            deg,\n            in_cover: vec![false; n],\n            current_cover_size: 0,\n            best_cover_size,\n            best_cover,\n        }\n    }\n    \n    fn greedy_lower_bound(&self) -> usize {\n        // Greedy matching: find a maximal matching\n        let mut matched = vec![false; self.n];\n        let mut count = 0;\n        for u in 0..self.n {\n            if self.active[u] && !matched[u] {\n                for &v in &self.adj[u] {\n                    if self.active[v] && !matched[v] {\n                        matched[u] = true;\n                        matched[v] = true;\n                        count += 1;\n                        break;\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n        }\n        count\n    }\n    \n    fn add_to_cover(&mut self, v: usize) -> Vec<(usize, bool)> {\n        let mut changed = vec![];\n        self.in_cover[v] = true;\n        self.active[v] = false;\n        self.current_cover_size += 1;\n        changed.push((v, true)); // (vertex, was_in_cover)\n        \n        let neighbors: Vec<usize> = self.adj[v].iter().filter(|&&u| self.active[u]).cloned().collect();\n        for u in neighbors {\n            self.deg[u] -= 1;\n            // Might cascade but we handle that in the B&B branching\n        }\n        // Also remove v from graph (set deg[v] = 0 effectively)\n        // We need to track the old degree changes\n        // Hmm, this is getting complex. Let me use a different approach.\n        changed\n    }\n}\n```\n\nActually, the B&B management is complex. Let me use a cleaner approach:\n\nI\'ll copy the state on each branch (since the kernel is small, this is affordable).\n\n```rust\nfn bb_solve(n: usize, adj: &[Vec<usize>], start: &Instant) -> Vec<bool> {\n    // Compute initial upper bound with greedy\n    let mut best = vec![false; n];\n    greedy_vc(n, adj, &mut best);\n    let mut best_size: usize = best.iter().filter(|&&b| b).count();\n    \n    // B&B\n    let active = vec![true; n];\n    let deg: Vec<usize> = (0..n).map(|v| adj[v].len()).collect();\n    let in_cover = vec![false; n];\n    \n    bb_recurse(\n        n, adj, active, deg, in_cover, 0,\n        &mut best_size, &mut best, start\n    );\n    \n    best\n}\n\nfn bb_recurse(\n    n: usize,\n    adj: &[Vec<usize>],\n    mut active: Vec<bool>,\n    mut deg: Vec<usize>,\n    mut in_cover: Vec<bool>,\n    current_size: usize,\n    best_size: &mut usize,\n    best: &mut Vec<bool>,\n    start: &Instant,\n) {\n    if start.elapsed().as_millis() > 9000 { return; }\n    \n    // Apply reduction rules\n    let mut extra_added = 0;\n    let mut to_process = VecDeque::new();\n    for v in 0..n {\n        if active[v] && deg[v] <= 1 {\n            to_process.push_back(v);\n        }\n    }\n    \n    loop {\n        let mut found = false;\n        // Degree-0: remove isolated\n        // Degree-1: add neighbor\n        while let Some(v) = to_process.pop_front() {\n            if !active[v] { continue; }\n            if deg[v] == 0 {\n                active[v] = false;\n                found = true;\n            } else if deg[v] == 1 {\n                if let Some(&u) = adj[v].iter().find(|&&u| active[u]) {\n                    in_cover[u] = true;\n                    extra_added += 1;\n                    active[u] = false;\n                    active[v] = false;\n                    for &w in &adj[u] {\n                        if active[w] {\n                            deg[w] -= 1;\n                            if deg[w] <= 1 {\n                                to_process.push_back(w);\n                            }\n                        }\n                    }\n                    found = true;\n                } else {\n                    active[v] = false;\n                    found = true;\n                }\n            }\n        }\n        if !found { break; }\n    }\n    \n    let current_size = current_size + extra_added;\n    \n    // Lower bound: greedy matching on remaining\n    let lb = greedy_matching_lb(n, adj, &active);\n    \n    if current_size + lb >= *best_size {\n        return; // prune\n    }\n    \n    // Find max-degree vertex\n    let v_opt = (0..n)\n        .filter(|&v| active[v] && deg[v] > 0)\n        .max_by_key(|&v| deg[v]);\n    \n    if let Some(v) = v_opt {\n        // Branch 1: include v\n        {\n            let mut new_active = active.clone();\n            let mut new_deg = deg.clone();\n            let mut new_cover = in_cover.clone();\n            \n            new_cover[v] = true;\n            new_active[v] = false;\n            for &u in &adj[v] {\n                if new_active[u] {\n                    new_deg[u] -= 1;\n                }\n            }\n            \n            bb_recurse(n, adj, new_active, new_deg, new_cover, current_size + 1, best_size, best, start);\n        }\n        \n        // Branch 2: exclude v (include all neighbors)\n        if start.elapsed().as_millis() < 9000 {\n            let mut new_active = active.clone();\n            let mut new_deg = deg.clone();\n            let mut new_cover = in_cover.clone();\n            \n            let neighbors: Vec<usize> = adj[v].iter().filter(|&&u| new_active[u]).cloned().collect();\n            let num_neighbors = neighbors.len();\n            \n            // Remove v\n            new_active[v] = false;\n            \n            // Add all neighbors to cover\n            for &u in &neighbors {\n                new_cover[u] = true;\n                new_active[u] = false;\n                for &w in &adj[u] {\n                    if new_active[w] {\n                        new_deg[w] -= 1;\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n            \n            bb_recurse(n, adj, new_active, new_deg, new_cover, current_size + num_neighbors, best_size, best, start);\n        }\n    } else {\n        // No more edges: we found a cover!\n        if current_size < *best_size {\n            *best_size = current_size;\n            *best = in_cover;\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\nWait, there are issues with the recursive B&B approach:\n1. Cloning vectors on each branch is expensive\n2. The reduction rules inside the recursion are complex\n\nFor small n (<=300), cloning Vec<bool> of size 300 and Vec<usize> of size 300 should be OK. Each clone is O(n) = O(300).\n\nBut the branching can have depth up to n, so we could have O(2^n) nodes... The key is pruning.\n\nActually, the number of B&B nodes is O(2^{n - k*}), where k* is the optimal cover size. With good lower bounds and the NT preprocessing, the remaining kernel should be manageable.\n\nLet me simplify the code and be more careful. Actually, the main issue is correctness. Let me trace through:\n\nIn `bb_recurse`:\n1. Apply reductions (degree-0 and degree-1)\n   - When we apply degree-1 reduction, we add the neighbor to cover and update degrees\n   - But we\'re modifying `active`, `deg`, `in_cover` directly (they\'re `mut` parameters)\n2. Compute lower bound\n3. Branch\n\nBut wait, after the reductions, we branch by cloning the current state. But the reductions already modified the state! So the clones will have the reduced state. That\'s correct.\n\nHowever, I need to make sure the reductions don\'t go into infinite loops. The while loop exits when `to_process` is empty and no new items were added. But `found` is only tracking if we dequeued something successfully; if to_process is empty and found is false, we break. But what if to_process is empty initially but there are still reducible vertices?\n\nLet me restructure:\n\n```rust\nloop {\n    let mut found = false;\n    // Check all active vertices for degree <= 1\n    for v in 0..n {\n        if active[v] {\n            if deg[v] == 0 {\n                active[v] = false;\n                found = true;\n            } else if deg[v] == 1 {\n                if let Some(&u) = adj[v].iter().find(|&&u| active[u]) {\n                    in_cover[u] = true;\n                    extra_added += 1;\n                    active[u] = false;\n                    active[v] = false;\n                    for &w in &adj[u] {\n                        if active[w] {\n                            deg[w] -= 1;\n                        }\n                    }\n                    found = true;\n                } else {\n                    active[v] = false;\n                    found = true;\n                }\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    if !found { break; }\n}\n```\n\nThis is O(n * iterations) and simple. For small n, this is fine.\n\nNow, there\'s a correctness issue: in the B&B, when we modify `active`, `deg`, `in_cover` in the reduction phase, and then clone them for branching, the reductions are "permanent" for the subproblem but we\'re branching from the reduced state. This is correct! The reductions are valid for any extension of the current partial solution.\n\nHowever, when I look at the code flow:\n- We enter `bb_recurse` with some state\n- We apply reductions directly to the passed-in state\n- We branch by cloning the modified state\n- After branching, we return\n- The caller\'s state is not restored (which is fine since we passed by value for active/deg/in_cover)\n\nWait, I\'m using `mut active: Vec<bool>` etc., which means they\'re passed by value (moved). So modifications are local to this function call. ✓\n\nBut in the branching, I clone the current state and pass it to recursive calls. Each recursive call modifies its own copy. ✓\n\nLet me also add the "if deg[v] > k (remaining budget), must include v" rule to prune better.\n\nActually, computing k (remaining budget = best_size - current_size - 1) and applying the rule is useful:\n- If deg[v] > k, v must be in the cover (otherwise we need to cover v\'s edges with v\'s neighbors, all of which must be in the cover, giving count > deg[v] > k, exceeding budget)\n- Hmm, actually the rule is: if deg[v] > k, add v to cover. Because if we don\'t add v, we must add all of v\'s neighbors (at least deg[v] > k vertices), but we only have k left.\n\nLet me add this rule to the reduction loop.\n\nAlso, I should add the LP lower bound for better pruning. The half-integral LP lower bound for the subgraph can be computed efficiently using greedy matching / Hopcroft-Karp. For the B&B on a small subgraph, even Hopcroft-Karp is fast.\n\nFor simplicity, let me use greedy matching as the lower bound (not optimal but fast):\n\n```rust\nfn greedy_matching_lb(n: usize, adj: &[Vec<usize>], active: &[bool]) -> usize {\n    let mut matched = vec![false; n];\n    let mut count = 0;\n    for u in 0..n {\n        if active[u] && !matched[u] {\n            for &v in &adj[u] {\n                if active[v] && !matched[v] {\n                    matched[u] = true;\n                    matched[v] = true;\n                    count += 1;\n                    break;\n                }\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    count\n}\n```\n\nThis gives a lower bound since any matching has at least 1 vertex from each matched edge, and matched edges form a valid lower bound.\n\nOK let me now write the complete, clean code. Removing v from cover is safe only if all edges incident to v are still covered, i.e., all v\'s neighbors are in the cover. Let me verify: if we remove v from cover, then for any edge (v, u), u must be in cover. If `adj[v].iter().all(|&u| in_cover[u])`, then yes, all of v\'s edges are covered by the other endpoint. ✓\n\nBut there\'s an issue: after removing v, some neighbor u of v might now also be redundant (if v was the only reason u was needed). We should re-check. The `while changed` loop handles this. ✓\n\nHowever, there\'s a subtlety: when we check `adj[v].iter().all(|&u| in_cover[u])`, we\'re checking in_cover[u] which might have changed in the same iteration. This could lead to incorrect removal if two vertices become redundant simultaneously.\n\nExample: v-u-w path. v and w are not in cover (no edges for them except to u). u is in cover.\n- v is not in example: triangle {0,1,2}, all in cover:\n- Check 0: adj[0]={1,2}, in_cover[1]=T, in_cover[2]=T → remove 0!\n- Now in_cover = {1, 2}\n- Check 1: adj[1]={0,2}, in_cover[0]=F → don\'t remove\n- Check 2: adj[2]={0,1}, in_cover[0]=F → don\'t remove\n- Stable: cover = {1, 2}\n\n✓ Optimal for triangle.\n\nBut wait, what if in the same pass we check 0 and remove it, then check 1:\n- adj[1]={0,2}: in_cover = {0, 1}\n- Check 0: adj[0]={1,2}, in_cover[1]=T, in_cover[2]=F → keep 0\n\nWe\'d get cover {0,1} which is also optimal. ✓\n\nBut what about: cover {0,1,2} and vertex 0 is being checked:\n- If we process 0 first and 2\'s cover status is still T, we remove 0\n- If we process 2 first and 0\'s cover status is still T, we remove 2\n- Either way we get the right answer.\n\nHowever, in a weird correctly.\n\nNow let me also think about the greedy_vc for large graphs. The greedy matching approach might not be great on structured graphs. An alternative is:\n\n**Greedy by degree**: repeatedly add the vertex with the highest degree to the cover, remove it and all its edges.\n\nThis is a log(m)-approximation for VC (treating it as a set cover problem). It might give better results than the 2-approx matching approach for some inputs, but it doesn\'t have a constant factor guarantee.\n\nI\'ll use the matching approach for the 2-approximation guarantee, and then apply redundancy removal.\n\nActually, there\'s an issue with the greedy matching approach when combined with the kernelization: after kernelization, the remaining active vertices have degree >= 2. I\'ll write the complete code:\n\nActually, I realize I should structure the code more carefully. No more planning - just code:\n\n```rust\nuse std::collections::VecDeque;\nuse std::io::{self, Read, Write, BufWriter};\nuse std::time::Instant;\n\nfn main() {\n    let builder = std::thread::Builder::new().stack_size(256 * 1024 * 1024);\n    let handler = builder.spawn(run).unwrap();\n    handler.join().unwrap();\n}\n\nfn run() {\n    let start = Instant::now();\n    let stdout = io::stdout();\n    let mut out = BufWriter::new(stdout.lock());\n    \n    let mut input = String::new();\n    io::stdin().read_to_string(&mut input).unwrap();\n    let mut it = input.split_ascii_whitespace();\n    \n    let n: usize = it.next().unwrap().parse().unwrap();\n    let m: usize = it.next().unwrap().parse().unwrap();\n    \n    let mut raw_edges: Vec<(usize, usize)> = Vec::with_capacity(m);\n    for _ in 0..m {\n        let u: usize = it.next().unwrap().parse().unwrap();\n        let v: usize = it.next().unwrap().parse().unwrap();\n        if u != v {\n            raw_edges.push((u.min(v), u.max(v)));\n        }\n    }\n    raw_edges.sort_unstable();\n    raw_edges.dedup();\n    \n    let mut adj: Vec<Vec<usize>> = vec![vec![]; n];\n    \n    // Phase 1: Kernelization\n    kernelize(n, &adj, &mut active, &mut deg, &mut in_cover);\n    \n    // Count kernel size\n    let n_kernel: usize = active.iter().filter(|&&a| a).count();\n    let m_kernel: usize = deg.iter().zip(active.iter()).filter(|(_, &a)| a).map(|(&d, _)| d).sum::<usize>() / 2;\n    \n    if n_kernel == 0 {\n        // Done by kernelization\n    } else if n_kernel <= 150_000 && m_kernel <= 2_000_000 {\n        // Use NT theorem\n        solve_with_nt(n, &adj, &mut active, &mut in_cover, &start);\n    } else {\n        // Greedy approximation\n        greedy_on_active(n, &adj, &active, &mut in_cover);\n        remove_redundant_active(n, &adj, &active, &mut in_cover);\n    }\n    \n    let cover: Vec<usize> = (0..n).filter(|&i| in_cover[i]).collect();\n    writeln!(out, "{}", cover.len()).unwrap();\n    if cover.is_empty() {\n        writeln!(out, "").unwrap();\n    } else {\n        let s: Vec<String> = cover.iter().map(|x| x.to_string()).collect();\n        writeln!(out, "{}", s.join(" ")).unwrap();\n    }\n}\n```\n\nNow let me implement each function:\n\n```rust\nfn kernelize(\n    n: usize,\n    adj: &[Vec<usize>],\n    active: &mut Vec<bool>,\n    deg: &mut Vec<usize>,\n    in_cover: &mut Vec<bool>,\n) {\n    let mut queue: VecDeque<usize> = (0..n)\n        .filter(|&v| deg[v] <= 1)\n        .collect();\n    \n    while let Some(v) = queue.pop_front() {\n        if !active[v] { continue; }\n        \n        if deg[v] == 0 {\n            active[v] = false;\n        } else {\n            // deg[v] == 1 (or was 1 when enqueued, might have changed)\n            // Re-check\n            if deg[v] != 1 { continue; So if deg[v] == 1 when enqueued and we dequeue it with active[v] == true, then deg[v] <= 1 at that point. If deg[v] == 0 now, we handle the degree-0 case. }\n    \n    let mut to_idx = vec![usize::MAX; n];\n    for (i, &v) in active_verts.iter().enumerate() {\n        to_idx[v] = i;\n    }\n    \n    // Build bipartite graph\n    // Left: indices 0..n_a (representing vertex vL)\n    // Right: indices 0..n_a (representing vertex vR)\n    // For each original edge (u,v) with both active:\n    //   add bipartite edge (u_idx, v_idx) [u in left, v in right]\n    //   add bipartite edge (v_idx, u_idx) [v in left, u in right]\n    \n    let mut bi_adj: Vec<Vec<usize>> = vec![vec![]; n_a];\n    for &v in &active_verts {\n        let vi = to_idx[v];\n        for &u in &adj[v] {\n            if active[u] {\n                let ui = to_idx[u];\n                bi_adj[vi].push(ui);\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    // Note: since adj is undirected, both (vi, ui) and (ui, vi) are added\n    \n    // Run Hopcroft-Karp\n    let (match_l, match_r) = hopcroft_karp(&bi_adj, n_a, n_a);\n    \n    // Find min vertex cover (König\'s theorem)\n    let (cover_l, cover_r) = konig_cover(&bi_adj, n_a, n_a, &match_l, &match_r);\n    \n    // Classify vertices\n    let mut x_half: Vec<usize> = vec![];\n    \n    for (i, &v) in active_verts.iter().enumerate() {\n        match (cover_l[i], cover_r[i]) {\n            (true, true) => {\n                in_cover[v] = true;\n                active[v] = false;\n            }\n            (false, false) => {\n                active[v] = false; // not in cover, and no edges to worry about\n            }\n            _ => {\n                x_half.push(v); // undecided\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    \n    let sub_n = x_half.len();\n    if sub_n == 0 { return; }\n    \n    // Build subgraph for x=1/2 vertices\n    let mut sub_to_idx = vec![usize::MAX; n];\n    for (i, &v) in x_half.iter().enumerate() {\n        sub_to_idx[v] = i;\n    }\n    \n    let mut sub_adj: Vec<Vec<usize>> = vec![vec![]; sub_n];\n    for &v in &x_half {\n        let vi = sub_to_idx[v];\n        for &u in &adj[v] {\n            // Only edges between x=1/2 vertices\n            if sub_to_idx[u] != usize::MAX {\n                let ui = sub_to_idx[u];\n                sub_adj[vi].push(ui);\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    // Dedup sub_adj (since adj might have had u appearing twice?)\n    // Actually adj was deduped earlier, so sub_adj should be fine\n    \n    // Solve subproblem\n    let sub_cover = if sub_n <= 400 && start.elapsed().as_millis() < 5000 {\n        bb_solve(sub_n, &sub_adj, start)\n    } else {\n        let mut sc = vec![false; sub_n];\n        greedy_vc(sub_n, &sub_adj, &mut sc);\n        remove_redundant(sub_n, &sub_adj, &mut sc);\n        sc\n    };\n    \n    for (i, &in_c) in sub_cover.iter().enumerate() {\n        if in_c {\n            in_cover[x_half[i]] = true;\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\nNow the Hopcroft-Karp:\n\n```rust\nfn hopcroft_karp(\n    adj: &[Vec<usize>],\n    n_left: usize,\n    n_right: usize,\n) -> (Vec<usize>, Vec<usize>) {\n    let nil = n_left;\n    let mut match_l = vec![usize::MAX; n_left];\n    let mut match_r = vec![usize::MAX; n_right];\n    let mut dist = vec![u32::MAX; n_left + 1];\n    \n    loop {\n        // BFS\n        let mut queue: VecDeque<usize> = VecDeque::new();\n        for u in 0..n_left {\n            if match_l[u] == usize::MAX {\n                dist[u] = 0;\n                queue.push_back(u);\n            } else {\n                dist[u] = u32::MAX;\n            }\n        }\n        dist[nil] = u32::MAX;\n        \n        while let Some(u) = queue.pop_front() {\n            if dist[u] < dist[nil] {\n                for &v in &adj[u] {\n                    let next = if match_r[v] == usize::MAX { nil } else { match_r[v] };\n                    if dist[next] == u32::MAX {\n                        dist[next] = dist[u] + 1;\n                        if next != nil {\n                            queue.push_back(next);\n                        }\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n        }\n        \n        if dist[nil] == u32::MAX { break; }\n        \n        let mut work = vec![0usize; n_left];\n        for u in 0..n_left {\n            if match_l[u] == usize::MAX {\n                dfs_hk(u, adj, &mut match_l, &mut match_r, &mut dist, &mut work, nil);\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    \n    (match_l, match_r)\n}\n\nfn dfs_hk(\n    u: usize,\n    adj: &[Vec<usize>],\n    match_l: &mut [usize],\n    match_r: &mut [usize],\n    dist: &mut [u32],\n    work: &mut [usize],\n    nil: usize,\n) -> bool {\n    if u == nil { return true; }\n    while work[u] < adj[u].len() {\n        let v = adj[u][work[u]];\n        let next = if match_r[v] == usize::MAX { nil } else { match_r[v] };\n        if dist[next] == dist[u] + 1\n            && dfs_hk(next, adj, match_l, match_r, dist, work, nil)\n        {\n            match_r[v] = u;\n            match_l[u] = v;\n            return true;\n        }\n        work[u] += 1;\n    }\n    dist[u] = u32::MAX;\n    false\n}\n```\n\nKönig\'s cover:\n\n```rust\nfn konig_cover(\n    adj: &[Vec<usize>],\n    n_left: usize,\n    n_right: usize,\n    match_l: &[usize],\n    match_r: &[usize],\n) -> (Vec<bool>, Vec<bool>) {\n    let mut in_z_l = vec![false; n_left];\n    let mut in_z_r = vec![false; n_right];\n    let mut queue: VecDeque<usize> = VecDeque::new();\n    \n    for u in 0..n_left {\n        if match_l[u] == usize::MAX {\n            in_z_l[u] = true;\n            queue.push_back(u);\n        }\n    }\n    \n    while let Some(u) = queue.pop_front() {\n        for &v in &adj[u] {\n            if !in_z_r[v] {\n                in_z_r[v] = true;\n                if match_r[v] != usize::MAX {\n                    let w = match_r[v];\n                    if !in_z_l[w] {\n                        in_z_l[w] = true;\n                        queue.push_back(w);\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    \n    let cover_l: Vec<bool> = (0..n_left).map(|u| !in_z_l[u]).collect();\n    let cover_r: Vec<bool> = (0..n_right).map(|v| in_z_r[v]).collect();\n    \n    (cover_l, cover_r)\n}\n```\n\nB&B solve:\n\n```rust\nfn bb_solve(n: usize, adj: &[Vec<usize>], start: &Instant) -> Vec<bool> {\n    // Initial greedy cover\n    let mut best = vec![false; }\n    \n    // Reduction rules\n    let mut extra = 0usize;\n    let mut changed = true;\n    while changed {\n        changed = false;\n        \n        // Rule 1: isolate\n        for v in 0..n {\n            if active[v] && deg[v] == 0 {\n                active[v] = false;\n                changed = true;\n            }\n        }\n        \n        // Rule 2: degree-1\n        for v in 0..n {\n            if active[v] && deg[v] == 1 {\n                let u = adj[v].iter().find(|&&u| active[u]).copied();\n                if let Some(u) = u {\n                    in_cover[u] = true;\n                    extra += 1;\n                    active[u] = false;\n                    active[v] = false;\n                    for &w in &adj[u] {\n                        if active[w] { deg[w] -= 1; }\n                    }\n                    changed = true;\n                } else {\n                    active[v] = false;\n                    changed = true;\n                }\n            }\n        }\n        \n        // Rule 3: high-degree (LP rule)\n        let budget = best_size.saturating_sub(current_size + extra + 1);\n        for v in 0..n {\n            if active[v] && deg[v] > budget {\n                in_cover[v] = true;\n                extra += 1;\n                active[v] = false;\n                for &w in &adj[v] {\n                    if active[w] { deg[w] -= 1; }\n                }\n                changed = true;\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    \n    let new_size = current_size + extra;\n    \n    // Lower bound check\n    let lb = greedy_matching_lb(n, adj, &active, &deg);\n    if new_size + lb >= *best_size {\n        return;\n    }\n    \n    // Find any uncovered edge (via max-degree vertex)\n    let v_opt = (0..n)\n        .filter(|&v| active[v] && deg[v] > 0)\n        .max_by_key(|&v| deg[v]);\n    \n    if let Some(v) = v_opt {\n        // Branch 1: include v\n        {\n            let mut na = active.clone();\n            let mut nd = deg.clone();\n            let mut nc = in_cover.clone();\n            nc[v] = true;\n            na[v] = false;\n            for &u in &adj[v] {\n                if na[u] { nd[u] -= 1; }\n            }\n            bb_recurse(n, adj, na, nd, nc, new_size + 1, best_size, best, start);\n        }\n        \n        // Branch 2: exclude v (include all neighbors)\n        if start.elapsed().as_millis() < 8000 {\n            let neighbors: Vec<usize> = adj[v].iter().filter(|&&u| active[u]).cloned().collect();\n            let k = neighbors.len();\n            \n            let mut na = active.clone();\n            let mut nd = deg.clone();\n            let mut nc = in_cover.clone();\n            \n            na[v] = false; }\n                }\n            }\n            \n            bb_recurse(n, adj, na, nd, nc, new_size + k, best_size, best, start);\n        }\n    } else {\n        // No active edges: cover is valid\n        if new_size < *best_size {\n            *best_size = new_size;\n            *best = in_cover;\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\nWait, there\'s an issue with `v_opt`: I\'m using `deg[v] > 0` but after deactivation, deg might not be updated for v itself. Let me modify that function:\n\n```rust\nfn greedy_matching_lb(n: usize, adj: &[Vec<usize>], active: &[bool], _deg: &[usize]) -> usize {\n    let mut matched = vec![false; n];\n    let mut count = 0;\n    for u in 0..n {\n        if active[u] && !matched[u] {\n            for &v in &adj[u] {\n                if active[v] && !matched[v] {\n                    matched[u] = true;\n Here\'s the complete solution:\n\nHere\'s another thought: after redundancy removal on a large graph, I can try a simple 2-1 swap:\n- For each vertex v in cover where deg_in_cover[v] = 0 (all v\'s active neighbors NOT in cover): but this is exactly what redundancy removal removes. Net gain: -1.\n\nThis requires: N(u) \\ cover = {w} AND N(v) \\ cover = {w}.\n\nIn other words: u and v have exactly one non-cover neighbor each, and it\'s the same vertex w.\n\nThis can be found in O(n + m) time:\n- For each w not in cover:\n  - Count how many cover neighbors u have N(u) \\ cover = {w}\n  - If >= 2 such u\'s: apply swap\n\nFor cover vertex u: N(u) \\ cover = {w} means u has exactly one non-cover neighbor, which is w. This means u\'s "unique" non-cover neighbor is w.\n\nAlgorithm:\n1. For each cover vertex u, find all non-cover neighbors\n2. If u has exactly 1 non-cover neighbor w: record (u, w)\n3. For each w: if it has >= 2 cover neighbors u1, u2 with their only non-cover neighbor being w:\n   - Remove u1, u2 from cover, add w → net gain -1\n\nThis is O(n + m) and can significantly improve the solution for some graph structures.\n\nLet me add this to the algorithm. But I need to be careful: after the swap, new opportunities might arise, so iterate until convergence.\n\nHere\'s the implementation:\n\n```rust\nfn swap_improve(\n    n: usize,\n    adj: &[Vec<usize>],\n    active: &[bool],\n    in_cover: &mut Vec<bool>,\n) {\n    loop {\n        // For each cover vertex, count non-cover neighbors\n        let unique_non_cover: Vec<Option<usize>> = (0..n).map(|u| {\n            if !active[u] || !in_cover[u] { return None; }\n            let non_cover_neighbors: Vec<usize> = adj[u].iter()\n                .filter(|&&v| active[v] && !in_cover[v])\n                .cloned()\n                .collect();\n            if non_cover_neighbors.len() == 1 {\n                Some(non_cover_neighbors[0])\n            } else {\n                None\n            }\n        }).collect();\n        \n        // For each non-cover vertex w, find cover vertices with w as unique non-cover neighbor\n        let mut w_to_us: Vec<Vec<usize>> = vec![vec![]; n];\n        for u in 0..n {\n            if let Some(w) = unique_non_cover[u] {\n                w_to_us[w].push(u);\n            }\n        }\n        \n        let mut improved = false;\n        for w in 0..n {\n            if !active[w] || in_cover[w] { continue; }\n            if w_to_us[w].len() >= 2 {\n                // Swap: remove w_to_us[w][0] and w_to_us[w][1] from cover, add w\n                let u1 = w_to_us[w][0];\n                let u2 = w_to_us[w][1];\n                in_cover[u1] = false;\n                in_cover[u2] = false;\n                in_cover[w] = true;\n                improved = true;\n                \n                // Run redundancy removal after each swap\n                // (since removing u1 and u2 might create new redundancies)\n                // Actually, applying redundancy removal after all swaps might be better\n                break; // Start over to recompute\n            }\n        }\n        \n        if !improved { break; }\n        \n        // Apply redundancy removal\n        remove_redundant_active(n, adj, active, in_cover);\n    }\n}\n```\n\nHmm, but after each swap, the `unique_non_cover` information changes.
